Lesson three, objection handling. I know you've been waiting for the objection handling, so let's get to it. Now, objection handling isn't really what you think it is or what most people think it is. So, what most people think objection handling is like some cool reframes you do and some some things you say and some cool things you saw on an Instagram or YouTube video. Or some people think objection handling is like okay it's some boxing match. It's not really about that. Essentially what objection handling is let's define objections first. What is an objection? The way we define it is objections are simply concerns. And everybody has concerns. People have concerns. It's fine. And so what we do is we're helping them overcome their own concern. That's essentially what it is. So the most important part is that we actually isolate and uncover the real concern of the prospect. Because a lot of times what the prospect says is the objection or the concern is not the real concern a lot of times. And so what I see is closers wasting a lot of time doing these crazy reframes on the wrong objection and then they end up wasting time or they lose the deal. Okay, so that's the first thing. And the next thing is that objection handling isn't about opening doors. It's about closing all the other doors. That way they only have one way to exit which is a sale. as an example as we talked about in the discovery process. We close all the other concerns. So the only thing left is what's moving forward and taking action. Now the problem I had was this when I was trying to get better at objection handling is that okay in the discovery at least there's something called a script. Okay. So, I follow this in objection handling though. What I found was that there isn't really per se a script. And especially when I got multiple different objections like some people say, "Hey, I got to talk to my partner. There a lot of money and just give me 24 hours to think about it." I just didn't know how to go about handling that. Okay, what do I handle first? What do I say? What do I do? Now, I'm just getting lost. I'm like, "Uh, okay." And then now I probably look uncertain. So, prospect doesn't see certainty in myself. and I end up just letting them go off the hook way too easily. So, I'll just end the call, maybe going to just like book a follow-up. They don't show up, they ghost me, and it was just a frustrating experience because I calculated how much money I'd be losing out on. And which is a fun exercise. I'd highly advise you to do this right now is write down how many maybe pull out a calculator. How many deals a week are you losing from objections that if you knew how to handle, if you had the right abilities, you could be overcoming them. So, type that in and type in an average commission you get per sale. I know it can vary. Take the average. That's a beautiful thing about a [ __ ] average, right? So now, long story short, people talk about there's all these different objections. Yes or no? I mean, in simple terms, there's mainly two different types of objections. One is the logistical, okay, logistical objections. And the other type is fear-based objections. What's the difference? Logistical is that they really want to do it. they would do it. It's just that there's a genuine valid reason holding them back from actually moving forward. As an example, they really want to do it. They would do it. Program is 5K. They only have 100 bucks in their bank account and their credit score is 400. It's probably going to be very hard, right? They want to do it. That'll be more of a logistical. But here's the thing though, because at times people say money is the only issue, but also a lot of times it's not really the real issue. There's some fear involved as well, right? So they could give us some smokec screen. So, we got to isolate that which we'll go over in the process. But yeah, that's a logistical and then there's the fear-based objection, right? So, fear-based objection is, yeah, I'm not sure if this will work. That's a lot of money. I don't know those kind of things. What if this doesn't work? I've been burned before. So, when we categorize into these different things, now it becomes okay in our mind whenever we get a concern objection, we can put them into different buckets. It becomes less overwhelming for us and things become a lot more clear. All right. Now within the fear objections, obviously there's different things a prospect can say which we'll go over. Okay, so here's the order of operations that we handle that objection. Okay, let's say someone gives you an objection doesn't matter what it is. What we want to do is we want to isolate the value first. Okay, and then we handle the money, the logistical money and then after that if we still have an objection, then we go into time. If they give us a time objection, meaning hey, I don't have the time to do that. And then we go into partner, whether it be spouse or business partner. And then if they give us fear then we go into fear or if they say think about it we handle that. Okay we want to go in this order. So again money time partner think about it slashfear in that order. The reason why we want to do it this way is because I'll give you a quick story. So, in the one of the companies that I was used to selling at, there was a guy and one of the reps on the team and he got an objection from a prospect and what he would do is he would pull out all these different fear reframes from his back pocket like, "Hey, this d and he was just hammering them." Now, that was good. And they would go on for about an hour and a half, two hours. And so, eventually the rep already missed the next call. He didn't want to miss another call. So, he's like, "Hey, listen. We do have financing. Do you want to do financing?" And the prospect goes, "You guys have financing?" And the salesperson goes, "Yeah." And the prospect goes, "Well, you should have told me an hour and a half ago, I would have done the financing." I was like, "Okay, well, do you want to do the financing?" "Yeah, I want to do the financing." And then the prospect gets approved for financing and they buy. So had he isolated the money, the logistical money, meaning that okay, could he do the financing, then he would have saved an hour and a half and then he already missed the call and maybe he would have missed the other call. He would have lost that deal if he kept going and just running out of time or just burning the lead. So we don't want to do that. So whenever we get an objection, we want to almost assume that the objection is logistical, not fear-based.
